This struct should be used in all places where a JSON-serialized\n// value is encrypted at-rest to maintain a consistent handling of data with security concerns.\n//\n// This struct should always be passed by reference.\ntype JSONEncryptable[T any] struct {\n\t*Encryptable\n}\n\n// NewUnencryptedJSON creates a new JSON encryptable from the given value.\nfunc NewUnencryptedJSON[T any](value T) (*JSONEncryptable[T], error) {\n\tserialized, err := json.Marshal(value)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn &JSONEncryptable[T]{Encryptable: NewUnencrypted(string(serialized))}, nil\n}\n\n// NewEncryptedJSON creates a new JSON encryptable an encrypted value and a relevant encryption key.\nfunc NewEncryptedJSON[T any](cipher, keyID string, key Key) *JSONEncryptable[T] {\n\treturn &JSONEncryptable[T]{Encryptable: NewEncrypted(cipher, keyID, key)}\n}\n\n// Decrypt decrypts and returns the underlying value as a T. This method may make an external API call\n// to decrypt the underlying encrypted value, but will memoize the result so that subsequent calls will\n// be cheap.\nfunc (e *JSONEncryptable[T]) Decrypt(ctx context.Context) (value T, _ error) {\n\tserialized, err := e.Encryptable.Decrypt(ctx)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn value, err\n\t}\n\n\tif err := json.Unmarshal([]byte(serialized), &value); err != nil {\n\t\treturn value, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn value, nil\n}\n\n// Set updates the underlying value.\nfunc (e *JSONEncryptable[T]) Set(value T) error {\n\tserialized, err := json.Marshal(value)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\te.mutex.Lock()\n\tdefer e.mutex.Unlock()\n\n\te.decrypted = &decryptedValue{string(serialized), nil}\n\te.encrypted = nil\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// DecryptJSON decrypts the encryptable value. This method may make an external\n// API call to decrypt the underlying encrypted value, but will memoize the result so that subsequent calls\n// will be cheap.\nfunc DecryptJSON[T any](ctx context.Context, e *JSONEncryptable[any]) (*T, error) {\n\tvar value T\n\n\tserialized, err := e.Encryptable.Decrypt(ctx)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tif err := json.Unmarshal([]byte(serialized), &value); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn &value, nil\n}\n","numLines":80,"startLine":1,"totalLines":80}}}

values for Type and Kind\n   143→//\n   144→// Types and Kinds are exposed through AsKind and AsType functions\n   145→// so that usages relying on the particular string of Type vs Kind\n   146→// will continue to behave correctly.\n   147→// The Type... and Kind... variables are left in place to avoid edge-case issues and to support\n   148→// commits that come in while the switch to Variant is ongoing.\n   149→// The Type... and Kind... variables are turned from consts into vars and use\n   150→// the corresponding Variant's AsType()/AsKind() functions.\n   151→// Consolidating Type... and Kind... into a single enum should decrease the smell\n   152→// and increase the usability and maintainability of this code.\n   153→//\n   154→// To add another external service variant\n   155→// 1. \"GitHubAppsStore\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"summary\": \"Sourcegraph's encryption-at-rest system is built on a layered abstraction in internal/encryption. The core Key interface (key.go) combines Encrypter and Decrypter, with a KeyVersion for identifying which key encrypted a value. Four key backend implementations exist: (1) NoopKey (noop.go) — passes plaintext through unchanged, used when encryption is disabled; (2) AWS KMS key (awskms/aws_kms.go) — uses envelope encryption where a per-value AES-256-GCM key is generated and the envelope key is wrapped by AWS KMS; (3) GCP Cloud KMS key (cloudkms/cloud_kms.go) — same envelope pattern using Google Cloud KMS; (4) Mounted key (mounted/key.go) — AES-256-GCM using a 32-byte secret loaded from an environment variable or file path. All three real backends use envelope encryption (envelope/envelope.go): a random 32-byte AES key encrypts the plaintext, and the envelope key itself is encrypted by the KMS/mounted key, with the whole structure serialized as base64(JSON) via wrapper/encryptedvalue.go (StorableEncryptedKey). An optional LRU cache (cache/cache.go) wraps any Key to avoid redundant decrypt API calls. The keyring (keyring/ring.go) holds a global Ring struct with named per-domain keys — BatchChangesCredentialKey, ExternalServiceKey, GitHubAppKey, UserExternalAccountKey, WebhookKey, WebhookLogKey, ExecutorSecretKey, SlackConfigurationKey, and OutboundWebhookKey — each independently configurable as any backend type. Init() watches site configuration and hot-reloads keys on change. The helpers MaybeEncrypt/MaybeDecrypt (helpers.go) are nil-safe wrappers that no-op if key is nil (encryption disabled) or if the stored keyID is empty (unmigrated plain-text value). Encrypted database fields use the Encryptable (encryptable.go) or JSONEncryptable[T] (json_encryptable.go) wrappers that lazily encrypt/decrypt and memoize results. Type aliases EncryptableCredential, EncryptableConfig, EncryptableSecret, EncryptableData, and EncryptableWebhookLogMessage map these wrappers to domain types. The following database tables/fields are encrypted at rest: user_credentials.credential (batch change user tokens, keyed by BatchChangesCredentialKey); site_credentials.credential (batch change site tokens, same key); external_services.config (code host configuration including API tokens, ExternalServiceKey); user_external_accounts.auth_data and user_external_accounts.data (OAuth tokens and profile data, UserExternalAccountKey); github_apps.private_key (GitHub App RSA private keys, GitHubAppKey); executor_secrets.value (CI/CD secrets, ExecutorSecretKey); webhooks.secret (incoming webhook signing secrets, WebhookKey); webhook_logs.request and webhook_logs.response (webhook HTTP payloads, WebhookLogKey); outbound_webhooks.url and outbound_webhooks.secret (outbound webhook config, OutboundWebhookKey); outbound_webhook_jobs.payload and outbound_webhook_logs.request/response/error (outbound webhook data, same key); slack_configurations.signing_secret and slack_configurations.bot_token (Slack integration credentials, SlackConfigurationKey). When encryption is fully disabled (no key configured, nil key), MaybeEncrypt stores the plaintext as-is with an empty keyID, and MaybeDecrypt returns the raw value without decrypting. When NoopKey is used, the 'encrypted' value is the plaintext itself stored verbatim.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":653,"cache_read_input_tokens":66086,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":653,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c225e1da-0562-4873-bbc8-4f69ab525324","uuid":"1050e3f6-c12a-408b-82a8-65102de9867a"}

\"GitHubAppsStore\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"summary\": \"Sourcegraph's encryption-at-rest system is built on a layered abstraction in internal/encryption. The core Key interface (key.go) combines Encrypter and Decrypter, with a KeyVersion for identifying which key encrypted a value. Four key backend implementations exist: (1) NoopKey (noop.go) — passes plaintext through unchanged, used when encryption is disabled; (2) AWS KMS key (awskms/aws_kms.go) — uses envelope encryption where a per-value AES-256-GCM key is generated and the envelope key is wrapped by AWS KMS; (3) GCP Cloud KMS key (cloudkms/cloud_kms.go) — same envelope pattern using Google Cloud KMS; (4) Mounted key (mounted/key.go) — AES-256-GCM using a 32-byte secret loaded from an environment variable or file path. All three real backends use envelope encryption (envelope/envelope.go): a random 32-byte AES key encrypts the plaintext, and the envelope key itself is encrypted by the KMS/mounted key, with the whole structure serialized as base64(JSON) via wrapper/encryptedvalue.go (StorableEncryptedKey). An optional LRU cache (cache/cache.go) wraps any Key to avoid redundant decrypt API calls. The keyring (keyring/ring.go) holds a global Ring struct with named per-domain keys — BatchChangesCredentialKey, ExternalServiceKey, GitHubAppKey, UserExternalAccountKey, WebhookKey, WebhookLogKey, ExecutorSecretKey, SlackConfigurationKey, and OutboundWebhookKey — each independently configurable as any backend type. Init() watches site configuration and hot-reloads keys on change. The helpers MaybeEncrypt/MaybeDecrypt (helpers.go) are nil-safe wrappers that no-op if key is nil (encryption disabled) or if the stored keyID is empty (unmigrated plain-text value). Encrypted database fields use the Encryptable (encryptable.go) or JSONEncryptable[T] (json_encryptable.go) wrappers that lazily encrypt/decrypt and memoize results. Type aliases EncryptableCredential, EncryptableConfig, EncryptableSecret, EncryptableData, and EncryptableWebhookLogMessage map these wrappers to domain types. The following database tables/fields are encrypted at rest: user_credentials.credential (batch change user tokens, keyed by BatchChangesCredentialKey); site_credentials.credential (batch change site tokens, same key); external_services.config (code host configuration including API tokens, ExternalServiceKey); user_external_accounts.auth_data and user_external_accounts.data (OAuth tokens and profile data, UserExternalAccountKey); github_apps.private_key (GitHub App RSA private keys, GitHubAppKey); executor_secrets.value (CI/CD secrets, ExecutorSecretKey); webhooks.secret (incoming webhook signing secrets, WebhookKey); webhook_logs.request and webhook_logs.response (webhook HTTP payloads, WebhookLogKey); outbound_webhooks.url and outbound_webhooks.secret (outbound webhook config, OutboundWebhookKey); outbound_webhook_jobs.payload and outbound_webhook_logs.request/response/error (outbound webhook data, same key); slack_configurations.signing_secret and slack_configurations.bot_token (Slack integration credentials, SlackConfigurationKey). When encryption is fully disabled (no key configured, nil key), MaybeEncrypt stores the plaintext as-is with an empty keyID, and MaybeDecrypt returns the raw value without decrypting. When NoopKey is used, the 'encrypted' value is the plaintext itself stored verbatim.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

`Encrypter`+`Decrypter`), `KeyVersion`, and `Secret` (an obfuscating wrapper that only exposes its value via an explicit `.Secret()` call)\n- **`encryptable.go`**: `Encryptable` — lazy encrypt/decrypt wrapper with memoization, used as the base for all encrypted DB fields\n- **`json_encryptable.go`**: `JSONEncryptable[T]` — generic variant for JSON-serialized values\n- **`helpers.go`**: `MaybeEncrypt`/`MaybeDecrypt` — nil-key-safe helpers; if no key is configured, data is stored/read as plaintext\n\n### Key Backend Implementations\n| Backend | File | Mechanism |\n|---|---|---|\n| **NoopKey** | `noop.go` | Returns plaintext unchanged (encryption disabled) |\n| **AWS KMS** | `awskms/aws_kms.go` | Envelope: random AES-256-GCM key encrypts plaintext; KMS wraps the envelope key |\n| **GCP Cloud KMS** | `cloudkms/cloud_kms.go` | Same envelope pattern via Google Cloud KMS |\n| **Mounted** | `mounted/key.go` | AES-256-GCM using a 32-byte secret from an env var or file |\n\n### Encryption Primitives\n- **`aeshelper/`**: AES-256-GCM encrypt/decrypt (32-byte key, random nonce)\n- **`envelope/`**: Generates a fresh 32-byte key per value, encrypts payload, returns the envelope key + ciphertext + nonce\n- **`wrapper/`**: Serializes `StorableEncryptedKey{Mechanism, KeyName, WrappedKey, Ciphertext, Nonce}` as `base64(JSON)`\n- **`cache/`**: Optional LRU cache around any `Key` to reduce KMS API calls\n\n### Keyring (`internal/encryption/keyring/ring.go`)\nThe global `Ring` struct holds one named key per domain, all hot-reloaded from site config via `Init()`:\n-
